  ***** BEGIN IOP MODEL SPECIFICATIONS *****

     The "New Case 2" IOP routine is being used:

          The absorption and scattering coefficients are determined by five components:

           Component 1 is pure water
           Component 2 is chlorophyll-bearing particles (includes absorption and small-particle phytoplankton scattering)
           Component 3 is total CDOM (assumed to be nonscattering)
           Component 4 is mineral particles (that do not covary with chlorophyll)
           Component 5 is large-particle phytoplankton scattering (absorption included in Component 2)
           The IOP printout also shows:
           Component 6 is the part of total CDOM that covaries with Chlorophyll
           Component 7 is the part of total CDOM that does not covary with Chlorophyll
                       (See the Technical Documentation or the source code for the bio-optical models that
                        convert these components concentrations to absorption and scattering coefficients.)

  Component 1 (pure water) specification:

     Pure water a and b values are computed as functions of temperature T and salinity S for
        T = 20.0 deg C and S = 35.0 PSU

     The phase function for IOP component  1 comes from file
        ../data/phase_functions/HydroLight/dpf_pure_H2O.txt

     The first  1 header records from data file ../data/phase_functions/HydroLight/dpf_pure_H2O.txt are:
        Phase function: A pure water phase function 0.06225*(1.0 + 0.835*cospsi^2) (created 27 Aug 2018 at 16:19)

          2 header records read

  Component 2 (chlorophyll-bearing particles) specification:

     The chlorophyll concentration is constant with depth with a value of     0.50 (mg/m^3)

     The scattering spectrum b(z,wavelength) for component 2 is calculated using a Power Law model:
          b = 0.3000 [concentration(z)]^(0.6200) * (550.0/wavelength)^(1.0000)

     The phase function for IOP component  2 comes from file
        ../data/phase_functions/HydroLight/dpf_Morel_Case1_small.txt

     The first  1 header records from data file ../data/phase_functions/HydroLight/dpf_Morel_Case1_small.txt are:
        Phase function: Morel's phase function for Case 1 water, small particles; for use in the "new Case 1" IOP model. (created 27 Aug 2018 at 16:34)

          2 header records read

  Component 3 (total CDOM) specification:

     The CDOM absorption at reference wavelength 440.0 nm is constant with depth with a value of     0.00 (1/m)

     The CDOM absorption spectrum for component 3 is calculated from an exponential model:
          a*(lambda) = 0.0000* exp[-0.0140*(lambda - 440.0)]

     CDOM is assumed to be non-scattering

  Component 4 (mineral particles that do not covary with chlorophyll) specification:

     The mineral particle concentration is constant with depth with a value of     0.10 (g/m^3)

     The concentration-specific absorption spectrum a*(lambda) for component 4 is the user-defined spectrum on file
        ../data/examples/minerals/astarmin_average.txt

     The concentration-specific scattering spectrum b*(lambda) for component 4 is the user-defined spectrum on file
        ../data/examples/minerals/bstarmin_average.txt

     The phase function for IOP component  4 comes from file
        ../data/phase_functions/HydroLight/dpf_Petzold_avg_particle.txt

     The first  1 header records from data file ../data/phase_functions/HydroLight/dpf_Petzold_avg_particle.txt are:
        Phase function: Petzold "average particle" phase function from Light and Water Table 3.10 (created 28 Aug 2018 at 16:28)

          2 header records read

     The phase function for IOP component  5 comes from file
        ../data/phase_functions/HydroLight/dpf_Morel_Case1_large.txt

     The first  1 header records from data file ../data/phase_functions/HydroLight/dpf_Morel_Case1_large.txt are:
        Phase function: Morel's phase function for Case 1 water, large particles; for use in the "new Case 1" IOP model. (created 27 Aug 2018 at 16:50)

          2 header records read

     The component concentrations at the requested output depths are:

           depth        Chl    a_CDOM(440)   minerals
             (m)     (mg/m^3)      (1/m)      (g/m^3)

  ***** END IOP MODEL SPECIFICATIONS *****


  ***** BEGIN INELASTIC SCATTER AND INTERNAL SOURCE SPECIFICATIONS *****

     Chlorophyll fluorescence is included in this run
        The chlorophyll absorption coefficient needed for the fluorescence calculation is obtained from the chlorophyll component of the IOP model
        The Chl fluorescence quantum efficiency set to  0.020

     CDOM fluorescence is included in this run.
        The CDOM absorption coefficient needed for the fluorescence calculation is obtained from the CDOM component of the IOP model

     Raman scattering is included in this run
        The Raman scattering coefficient is  2.60E-04 1/m at reference wavelength  488.0 nm
        The Raman scattering coefficient depends on the EXCITATION wavelength as
           (reference wavelength/excitation wavelength)^5.30

  ***** END INELASTIC SCATTER AND INTERNAL SOURCE SPECIFICATIONS *****


  ***** BEGIN ATMOSPHERIC MODEL SPECIFICATIONS *****

     Normalized sky radiances are computed using sky model "sky_radiance_HC" (Harrison and Coombes normalized sky radiances)

     The cloud fraction is cloud =  0.0 (0 for a clear sky to 1 for a heavy overcast)

     The sun is placed in quad Q(r,s) = Q( 7, 1) centered at (theta, phi) = (30.000,  0.000)

     Diffuse and direct sky irradiances are computed using RADTRANX
        (The Gregg and Carder RADTRAN model eXtended to 300-1000 nm)
     The RADTRANX clear-sky irradiances are adjusted for cloudiness by the model of Kasten and Czeplak

     Parameter values used in the RADTRANX model:
          Solar zenith    angle =   30.0  degrees
          Solar azimuthal angle =    0.0  degrees (downwind is 0)
          Sea level pressure    =   29.9  in. mercury
          Day of year not set (mean earth-sun distance used)
          Air mass type         =    1.0
          Relative humidity     =   80.0  %
          Precipitable water    =    2.5  cm
          24-hr wind speed      =    5.0  m/sec
          Current wind speed    =    5.0  m/sec
          Visibility            =   15.0  km
          Total ozone           =  300.0  Dobson units

     Irradiances are computed just above the sea surface

     Aerosol parameters from the Navy aerosol model used by RADTRANX:
          alpha                    =   0.2174
          beta                     =   0.2289
          asymmetry parameter      =   0.7892
          single scattering albedo =   0.9928

     Aerosol optical thickness at 550 nm =    0.261
 

  ***** END ATMOSPHERIC MODEL SPECIFICATIONS *****


  ***** BEGIN AIR-WATER SURFACE SPECIFICATIONS *****

     The air-water surface is for a wind speed of  5.0 m/s

     The water real index of refraction is constant for all wavelengths with the value of 1.340

     The surface wave model is Cox-Munk with azimuthally averaged slope statistics

     The azimuthal angle of the sun relative to the downwind direction is sunphi =   0.0 deg

  ***** END AIR-WATER SURFACE SPECIFICATIONS *****


  ***** BEGIN BOTTOM BOUNDARY SPECIFICATIONS *****

     The bottom boundary is an infinitely deep, homogeneous, elastically scattering water body below depth  10.00 m
        The reflectance of the water column below  10.00 m is modeled by a non-Lambertian BRDF computed from the IOPs at  10.00 m.

     The actual depth at which the infinitely deep bottom boundary condition will be applied 
        will be determined at run time from the IOPs to ensure a good solution at the requested output depths

  ***** END BOTTOM BOUNDARY SPECIFICATIONS *****

     No files were read with data ranges less than the run depth and wavelength ranges.

  ***** END WARNING MESSAGES FOR INPUT DATA FILES *****
